        <!-- Only show dros in supplementary section for intermediate-dictionary/kids dictionary words -> https://merriam.atlassian.net/browse/MWSITE-9211 -->
        
                                <div class="entry-uros ">
                
      <div class="uro ">
      <div class="uro-content">
                                                      <span class="fw-bold ure">goodish</span>
                        <div class="prons-entries-list d-inline-flex align-items-center">
                                                                          <a class="play-pron-v2 text-decoration-none prons-entry-list-item d-flex align-items-center justify-content-center badge mw-badge-gray-300" data-lang="en_us" data-file="good0004" data-dir="g" href="/dictionary/good?pronunciation&lang=en_us&dir=g&amp;file=good0004" data-url="https://www.merriam-webster.com/dictionary/good?pronunciation&lang=en_us&dir=g&amp;file=good0004" data-title="How to pronounce good (audio)" title="How to pronounce good (audio)">ˈgu̇-dish&nbsp;<img class="svg" src="/dist-cross-dungarees/2025-03-01--01-08-40-34ndm/images/svg/audio-pron-redesign.svg" alt="How to pronounce good (audio)"></a>
                          </div>
                                      <span class="fw-bold fl">adjective</span>
                                                                                                        </div>
    </div>
                    </div>
        
                
                
                
        
                
    </div>
    
                                                                                                                                <div id="usage-discussion-1-anchor" class="usage_notes content-section-with-header pt-5">
    <div id="usage-discussion-anchor"></div>
    <div class="content-section-sub-header">
                    <img class="pe-2" src="/dist-cross-dungarees/2025-03-01--01-08-40-34ndm/images/svg/redesign/pen-icon.svg" role="presentation" alt="" />
                <span class="mw_t_parahw">Good</span> vs. <span class="mw_t_parahw">Well</span>: Usage Guide    </div> 
    <div class="content-section-body">
        <p>
  <div class="pb-2 mt-5">    
    <p>An old notion that it is wrong to say "I feel good" in reference to health still occasionally appears in print. The origins of this notion are obscure, but they seem to combine someone's idea that <em class="mw_t_it">good</em> should be reserved to describe virtue and uncertainty about whether an adverb or an adjective should follow <em class="mw_t_it">feel.</em> Today nearly everyone agrees that both <em class="mw_t_it">good</em> and <em class="mw_t_it">well</em> can be predicate adjectives after <em class="mw_t_it">feel.</em> Both are used to express good health, but <em class="mw_t_it">good</em> may connote good spirits in addition to good health.</p>  </div>
 </p>
    </div>
</div>

                                                                                                                                <div id="usage-discussion-3-anchor" class="usage_notes content-section-with-header pt-5">
    <div id="usage-discussion-anchor"></div>
    <div class="content-section-sub-header">
                    <img class="pe-2" src="/dist-cross-dungarees/2025-03-01--01-08-40-34ndm/images/svg/redesign/pen-icon.svg" role="presentation" alt="" />
                <span class="mw_t_parahw">Good</span> vs. <span class="mw_t_parahw">Well</span>: Usage Guide    </div> 
    <div class="content-section-body">
        <p>
  <div class="pb-2 mt-5">    
    <p>Adverbial <em class="mw_t_it">good</em> has been under attack from the schoolroom since the 19th century. Insistence on <em class="mw_t_it">well</em> rather than <em class="mw_t_it">good</em> has resulted in a split in connotation: <em class="mw_t_it">well</em> is standard, neutral, and colorless, while <em class="mw_t_it">good</em> is emotionally charged and emphatic. This makes <em class="mw_t_it">good</em> the adverb of choice in sports.</p>  </div>
  <div class=""> 
          <div class="sub-content-thread mb-3">
      <span class="thread-anchor"></span>
        <div class="threaded-content ps-3">
          


          <span class="sub-content-thread ex-sent  first-child t has-aq sents">
      <span class="thread-anchor"></span>
      <span class="d-block thread-anchor-content pb-1">
         
                        &quot;I'm seeing the ball real <em class="mw_t_it">good</em>&quot; is what you hear      </span>
    </span>
        <span class="ex-sent aq has-aq sents">
        
<span class="aq">
            <span class="auth"><span class="me-2 mw-mdash-gold"><span class="mdash mdash-silent">&mdash;</span><img class="svg" src="/dist-cross-dungarees/2025-03-01--01-08-40-34ndm/images/svg/mdash-gold.svg" alt="" role="presentation" /></span>Roger Angell</span>      </span>    </span>
  
        </div>
      </div> 
      </div>
  <div class="pb-2 mt-5">    
    <p>In such contexts as</p>  </div>
  <div class=""> 
          <div class="sub-content-thread mb-3">
      <span class="thread-anchor"></span>
        <div class="threaded-content ps-3">
          


          <span class="sub-content-thread ex-sent  first-child t has-aq sents">
      <span class="thread-anchor"></span>
      <span class="d-block thread-anchor-content pb-1">
         
                        listen up. And listen <em class="mw_t_it">good</em>      </span>
    </span>
        <span class="ex-sent aq has-aq sents">
        
<span class="aq">
            <span class="auth"><span class="me-2 mw-mdash-gold"><span class="mdash mdash-silent">&mdash;</span><img class="svg" src="/dist-cross-dungarees/2025-03-01--01-08-40-34ndm/images/svg/mdash-gold.svg" alt="" role="presentation" /></span>Alex Karras</span>      </span>    </span>
  
        </div>
      </div> 
          <div class="sub-content-thread mb-3">
      <span class="thread-anchor"></span>
        <div class="threaded-content ps-3">
          


          <span class="sub-content-thread ex-sent  first-child t has-aq sents">
      <span class="thread-anchor"></span>
      <span class="d-block thread-anchor-content pb-1">
         
                        lets fly with his tomatoes before they can flee. He gets Clarence <em class="mw_t_it">good</em>      </span>
    </span>
        <span class="ex-sent aq has-aq sents">
        
<span class="aq">
            <span class="auth"><span class="me-2 mw-mdash-gold"><span class="mdash mdash-silent">&mdash;</span><img class="svg" src="/dist-cross-dungarees/2025-03-01--01-08-40-34ndm/images/svg/mdash-gold.svg" alt="" role="presentation" /></span>Charles Dickinson</span>      </span>    </span>
  
        </div>
      </div> 
      </div>
  <div class="pb-2 mt-5">    
    <p><em class="mw_t_it">good</em> cannot be adequately replaced by <em class="mw_t_it">well.</em> Adverbial <em class="mw_t_it">good</em> is primarily a spoken form; in writing it occurs in reported and fictional speech and in generally familiar or informal contexts.</p>  </div>
 </p>
    </div>

                                <h2>Word History</h2>
                            </div>
                            <div class="content-section-body">
                                                                    <div class="etymology-content-section">
                                        <div class="content-section-sub-header">Etymology</div>
                                                                                                                                    <p class="function-label">Adjective, Noun, and Adverb</p>
                        <p class="et">
                Middle English, from Old English <em class="mw_t_it">gōd</em>; akin to Old High German <em class="mw_t_it">guot</em> good, Middle High German <em class="mw_t_it">gatern</em> to unite, Sanskrit <em class="mw_t_it">gadhya</em> what one clings to            </p>
                                                                                        </div>
                                
                                                                                                    <div class="first-known-content-section">
                                        <div class="content-section-sub-header">First Known Use</div>
                                                                                        <p class="function-label">Adjective</p>
<p class="ety-sl pb-3" data-entry-id="1">before the 12th century, in the meaning defined at <a href="#h1">sense 1a(1)</a></p>                                                                                        <p class="function-label">Noun</p>
<p class="ety-sl pb-3" data-entry-id="2">before the 12th century, in the meaning defined at <a href="#h2">sense 1a</a></p>                                                                                        <p class="function-label">Adverb</p>
<p class="ety-sl pb-3" data-entry-id="3">13th century, in the meaning defined at <a href="#h3">sense 1</a></p>                                                                            </div>

            <span class="sd">specifically</span>                
          
                                                      <span class="dtText"><strong class="mw_t_bc">: </strong>furniture, furnishings, and personal effects used in a dwelling as defined by section 7-209 of the Uniform Commercial Code</span>                                      
            </div>      </div>          </span>
  </div>
            </div>
              </div>
      </div>                      
<div class="sub">
  <span class="mdash">&mdash;</span>
            <span class="shw">mobile goods</span>
                <div class="sub">
                  
<div class="vg">
                    <div class="sb no-sn">
      <span class="sb-0">
              <div class="sense no-subnum">

              <span class="dt ">
            
          
            
                                                <span class="dtText"><strong class="mw_t_bc">: </strong>goods as formerly defined in section 9-103 of the Uniform Commercial Code that are mobile, are of a type (as vehicles) usually used in more than one jurisdiction, are not covered by a certificate of title, and are either the equipment of a debtor or inventory leased by a debtor</span>                                      
      

        </span>

      </div>          </span>
  </div>
            </div>
              </div>
      </div>                      
<div class="sub">
  <span class="mdash">&mdash;</span>
            <span class="shw">ordinary goods</span>
                <div class="sub">
                  
<div class="vg">
                    <div class="sb no-sn">
      <span class="sb-0">
              <div class="sense no-subnum">

              <span class="dt ">
            
          
            
                                                <span class="dtText"><strong class="mw_t_bc">: </strong>goods as formerly defined by section 9-103 of the Uniform Commercial Code that are anything other than those covered by a certificate of title, mobile goods, or minerals</span>                                      
      

        </span>

      </div>          </span>
  </div>
            </div>
              </div>
      </div>                      
<div class="sub">
  <span class="mdash">&mdash;</span>
            <span class="shw">producer goods</span>
                <div class="sub">
                  
<div class="vg">
                    <div class="sb no-sn">
      <span class="sb-0">
              <div class="sense no-subnum">

              <span class="dt ">
            
          
            
                                                <span class="dtText"><strong class="mw_t_bc">: </strong>goods (as tools and raw materials) used to produce other goods and satisfy human wants only indirectly</span>                                      
      

        </span>

      </div>          </span>
  </div>
            </div>

                        </div>
